        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646"><meta property="og:title" content="SnCo Nanoparticles Loaded in Hollow Carbon Spheres Interlinked by N-Doped Carbon Fibers for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646/asset/images/acs.inorgchem.3c00646.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="The development of Sn-based materials with electrochemically inactive matrices is a novel strategy to alleviate the volume expansion and giant structure strain/stress during the sodiation/desodiation process. In this work, a freestanding membrane based on the unique bean pod-like host composed by nitrogen-doped carbon fibers and hollow carbon spheres (HCSs) encapsulated with SnCo nanoparticles is synthesized by electrospinning (B-SnCo/NCFs). In this unique bean pod-like structure, Sn acts as a host for Na+ storage, while the Co plays the important role of an electrochemically inactive matrix that can not only buffer the volume variations but also inhibit aggregation and particle growth of the Sn phase during the electrochemical Na–Sn alloying process. Meanwhile, the introduction of hollow carbon spheres can not only provide enough sufficient void space to withstand the volume expansion during the (de)sodiation processes but also improve the conductivity of the anode along the carbon fibers. Furthermore, the B-SnCo/NCF freestanding membrane can increase the contact area between the active material and the electrolyte, which can provide more active sites during the cycling process. When used as an anode material for Na-ion batteries, the freestanding B-SnCo/NCF anode exhibits an outstanding rate capacity of 243.5 mA h g–1 at 1.6 A g–1and an excellent specific capacity of 351 mA h g–1 at 0.1 A g–1 for 300 cycles."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646/asset/images/acs.inorgchem.3c00646.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/1122814~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="93187d14ef1a0762-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="93187d14ef1a0762-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: '6d0cc841-cf23-462f-9d3d-949131f2c2ad'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

img{border:0}.a2a_button_facebook_like iframe{max-width:none}</style><script charset="utf-8" src="https://pubs.acs.org/products/achs/releasedAssets/js/article-dc83549a302b9ecf025f.js"></script><script charset="utf-8" async="" src="https://script.hotjar.com/modules.f98993dba31a932bc912.js"></script><script id="yui__dyn_0" type="text/javascript" src="https://www2.snapengage.com/chatjs/ServiceGetConfig?w=921a4ec7-cecf-43a6-afa5-6cd1346520b1"></script><script charset="utf-8" src="https://pubs.acs.org/products/achs/releasedAssets/js/requestidlecallback-polyfill-f5170b9de43ccc25622c.js"></script><script charset="utf-8" src="https://pubs.acs.org/products/achs/releasedAssets/js/vendors~lazy-imports-c0b82d66d33565b4cebe.js"></script><script charset="utf-8" src="https://pubs.acs.org/products/achs/releasedAssets/js/lazy-imports-6922fe6a4ca6b2e0cd9a.js"></script><script type="text/javascript" src="/specs/products/achs/releasedAssets/public/mathjax-0a9852ad89643b94fe5099b753f6a294/MathJax.js?config=TeX-AMS-MML_HTMLorMML"></script><script type="text/x-mathjax-config;executed=true">MathJax.Hub.Config({
            menuSettings: {
                zoom: "Click",
                zscale: "150%"
            },
            SVG: {
                fonts: ["STIX-Web"],
                linebreaks: { automatic: true },
            },
            "HTML-CSS": {
                fonts: ["STIX"],
                linebreaks: { automatic: true },
                scale: 90,
            },
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("mml Jax Ready", function () {
            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;
            MML.mi.prototype.setTeXclass = function (prev) {
                this.getPrevClass(prev);
                return this;
            };
            MML.mfrac.Augment({
                setTeXclass: function (prev) {
                    this.getPrevClass(prev);
                    for (var i = 0, m = this.data.length; i < m; i++) {
                        if (this.data[i]) this.data[i].setTeXclass();
                    }
                    return this;
                }
            });
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("SVG Jax Ready", function () {
            var FONT = MathJax.OutputJax.SVG.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-Web-variant"] || MathJax.OutputJax.SVG.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-variant"];
            delete MathJax.ElementJax.mml.mo.prototype.remapChars['°'];
            if (FONT) {
                FONT.remap[0xB0]= [0x25E6, "normal"];
                FONT.remap[0x2A]= [0x2217, "normal"];
            }

        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("MathML Jax Ready", function () {
            var PARSE = MathJax.InputJax.MathML.Parse;
            var ADD = PARSE.prototype.AddChildren;
            PARSE.Augment({
                AddChildren: function (mml, node) {
                    ADD.call(this, mml, node);
                    if (mml.type === 'mrow') {
                        var first = mml.data[0], last = mml.data[mml.data.length-1];
                        if (mml.open && !mml.data[0].Get('stretchy')) delete mml.open;
                        if (mml.close && !mml.data[mml.data.length - 1].Get('stretchy')) delete mml.close;
                    }
                }
            });
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("HTML-CSS Jax Ready", function () {
            var HTMLCSS = MathJax.OutputJax['HTML-CSS'];
            var DELIMITERS = HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.DELIMITERS;
            var FONT = HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-variant"] || HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-Web-variant"]

            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;

            MML.mrow.Augment({
              _HTMLlineBreaks: MML.mrow.prototype.HTMLlineBreaks,
              HTMLlineBreaks: function (span) {

                if (this.parent.linebreakContainer && this.Get("display") === "inline") return false;
                return this._HTMLlineBreaks(span);
              }
            });


            DELIMITERS[0x0305] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x00AF};
            DELIMITERS[0x033F] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x003D};
            DELIMITERS[0x20E1] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x2194};

            if (FONT) {
                FONT.remap[0xB0]= [0x25E6, "normal"];
                FONT.remap[0x2A]= [0x2217, "normal"];
            }

            delete MathJax.ElementJax.mml.mo.prototype.remapChars['°'];
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("HTML-CSS multiline Ready", function () {
            var HTMLCSS = MathJax.OutputJax["HTML-CSS"];
            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;
            var PENALTY = MML.mbase.prototype.HTMLlinebreakPenalty;

            MML.msqrt.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mroot.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mfrac.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mspace.Augment({
                defaultDef: {
                    indentalign: MML.INDENTALIGN.AUTO,
                    indentshift: "0",
                    indenttarget: "",
                    indentalignfirst: MML.INDENTALIGN.INDENTALIGN,
                    indentshiftfirst: MML.INDENTSHIFT.INDENTSHIFT,
                    indentalignlast: MML.INDENTALIGN.INDENTALIGN,
                    indentshiftlast: MML.INDENTSHIFT.INDENTSHIFT
                },
                HTMLbetterBreak: function (info,state) {
                    if (info.values && info.values.id === this.spanID) {return false}
                    var values = this.getValues(
                        "linebreak",
                        "indentalign","indentshift",
                        "indentalignfirst","indentshiftfirst",
                        "indentalignlast","indentshiftlast"
                    );
                    var linebreakValue = values.linebreak;
                    if (!linebreakValue || this.hasDimAttr()) {
                        linebreakValue = MML.LINEBREAK.AUTO;
                    }
                    var W = info.scanW, span = this.HTMLspanElement(), w = span.bbox.w;
                    if (span.style.paddingLeft) {w += HTMLCSS.unEm(span.style.paddingLeft)}
                    if (W - info.shift === 0) {return false} // don't break at zero width
                    var offset = HTMLCSS.linebreakWidth - W;

                    if (state.n === 0 && (values.indentshiftfirst !== state.VALUES.indentshiftfirst ||
                        values.indentalignfirst !== state.VALUES.indentalignfirst)) {
                        var align = this.HTMLgetAlign(state,values),
                            shift = this.HTMLgetShift(state,values,align);
                        offset += (info.shift - shift);
                    }

                    var penalty = Math.floor(offset / HTMLCSS.linebreakWidth * 1000);
                    if (penalty < 0) {penalty = PENALTY.toobig - 3*penalty}
                    penalty += info.nest * PENALTY.nestfactor;

                    var linebreak = PENALTY[linebreakValue]||0;
                    if (linebreakValue === MML.LINEBREAK.AUTO && w >= PENALTY.spacelimit &&
                        !this.mathbackground && !this.background)
                    {linebreak = [(w+PENALTY.spaceoffset)*PENALTY.spacefactor]}
                    if (!MathJax.Object.isArray(linebreak)) {
                        if (linebreak || offset >= 0) {penalty = linebreak * info.nest}
                    } else {penalty = Math.max(1,penalty + linebreak[0] * info.nest)}

                    if (penalty >= info.penalty) {return false}
                    info.penalty = penalty; info.values = values; info.W = W; info.w = w;
                    values.lineleading = state.VALUES.lineleading;
                    values.linebreakstyle = "before"; values.id = this.spanID;
                    return true;
                }
            });


            
            PENALTY.goodbreak = [-400];

        });</script><style type="text/css">.MathJax_Hover_Frame {border-radius: .25em; -webkit-border-radius: .25em; -moz-border-radius: .25em; -khtml-border-radius: .25em; box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; -webkit-box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; -moz-box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; -khtml-box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; border: 1px solid #A6D ! important; display: inline-block; position: absolute}

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="93187d14ef1a0762-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'inorganic_chemistry';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/inorganic_chemistry/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/inorganic_chemistry/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

data-references="https://pubs.acs.org/action/ajaxShowEnhancedAbstract?doi=10.1021%2Facs.inorgchem.3c00646&amp;ajax=true" data-enable-mathjax="true" vocab="http://schema.org/" typeof="ScholarlyArticle" class="article--latest"><div class="figure-viewer"><div class="figure-viewer_row"><div class="figure-viewer_col loop-trap"><div aria-live="polite" aria-atomic="true" class="figure-viewer_modal"><a href="/action/showCitFormats?doi=10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646&amp;href=/doi/10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646" title="Cite This" class="figure-viewer-cite-this-link"><i <script nonce="93187d14ef1a0762-SJC">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "inocaj";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "SnCo Nanoparticles Loaded in Hollow Carbon Spheres Interlinked by N-Doped Carbon Fibers for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "SnCo Nanoparticles Loaded in Hollow Carbon Spheres Interlinked by N-Doped Carbon Fibers for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "SnCo Nanoparticles Loaded in Hollow Carbon Spheres Interlinked by N-Doped Carbon Fibers for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "SnCo Nanoparticles Loaded in Hollow Carbon Spheres Interlinked by N-Doped Carbon Fibers for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "SnCo Nanoparticles Loaded in Hollow Carbon Spheres Interlinked by N-Doped Carbon Fibers for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "SnCo Nanoparticles Loaded in Hollow Carbon Spheres Interlinked by N-Doped Carbon Fibers for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "SnCo Nanoparticles Loaded in Hollow Carbon Spheres Interlinked by N-Doped Carbon Fibers for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "SnCo Nanoparticles Loaded in Hollow Carbon Spheres Interlinked by N-Doped Carbon Fibers for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "SnCo Nanoparticles Loaded in Hollow Carbon Spheres Interlinked by N-Doped Carbon Fibers for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

class="articleMetrics_count"><h2>Citations</h2><div class="articleMetrics-val"><a href="#citeThis" class="internalNav">5</a></div></div></div></div><div class="articleMetrics_about"><div class="base data-db-target-of="aboutArticleMetrics" id="about-article-metrics" class="dropBlock__holder"><button class="articleMetrics_close"> <i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-close_thin"></i><span Find more information on<a href="https://help.altmetric.com/support/solutions/articles/6000233311-how-is-the-altmetric-attention-score-calculated"> the Altmetric Attention Score and how the score is calculated.</a></p></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646/asset/images/medium/ic3c00646_0008.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646/asset/images/large/ic3c00646_0008.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">The development of Sn-based materials with electrochemically inactive matrices is a novel strategy to alleviate the volume expansion and giant structure strain/stress during the sodiation/desodiation process. In this work, a freestanding membrane based on the unique bean pod-like host composed by nitrogen-doped carbon fibers and hollow carbon spheres (HCSs) encapsulated with SnCo nanoparticles is synthesized by electrospinning (B-SnCo/NCFs). In this unique bean pod-like structure, Sn acts as a host for Na<sup>+</sup> storage, while the Co plays the important role of an electrochemically inactive matrix that can not only buffer the volume variations but also inhibit aggregation and particle growth of the Sn phase during the electrochemical Na–Sn alloying process. Meanwhile, the introduction of hollow carbon spheres can not only provide enough sufficient void space to withstand the volume expansion during the (de)sodiation processes but also improve the conductivity of the anode along the carbon fibers. Furthermore, the B-SnCo/NCF freestanding membrane can increase the contact area between the active material and the electrolyte, which can provide more active sites during the cycling process. When used as an anode material for Na-ion batteries, the freestanding B-SnCo/NCF anode exhibits an outstanding rate capacity of 243.5 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 1.6 A g<sup>–1</sup>and an excellent specific capacity of 351 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup> for 300 cycles.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D7393%26pageCount%3D10%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DShengqiang%2BZhang%252C%2BJie%2BDang%252C%2BChengxin%2BLiu%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D62%26issueNum%3D19%26contentID%3Dacs.inorgchem.3c00646%26title%3DSnCo%2BNanoparticles%2BLoaded%2Bin%2BHollow%2BCarbon%2BSpheres%2BInterlinked%2Bby%2BN-Doped%2BCarbon%2BFibers%2Bfor%2BHigh-Performance%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26numPages%3D10%26pa%3D%26issn%3D0020-1669%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Dinocaj%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D7402%26publicationDate%3DMay%2B2023" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2023 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">
                                        Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291517&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Batteries"> Batteries </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291371&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrodes"> Electrodes </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292506&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Materials"> Materials </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291009&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Nanofibers"> Nanofibers </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=290920&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Nanoparticles"> Nanoparticles </a></li></ul></div></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody" style="width: 384px;"><div class="hlFld-Abstract synopsis"><h2>Synopsis</h2><span><p class="articleBody_abstractText">In this work, we describe the synthesis of a freestanding membrane based on the unique bean pod-like host composed by nitrogen-doped carbon fibers and hollow carbon spheres encapsulated with SnCo nanoparticles by electrospinning. Due to the synergy of the porous nitrogen-doped carbon fibers and SnCo nanoparticles, the B-SnCo/NCFs display excellent performance when used in an Na-ion battery.</p></span></div><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">1.  Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">Secondary batteries, as one of the sources of green energy, play a crucial role in the decarbonization of the worldwide economies. Sustainable and safe green batteries will facilitate reduction of the environmental pollution caused by traditional chemical fuels and decrease the consumption of natural resources. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref1" aria-label="reference 1">(1)</a> Recently, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), with the advantages of the same reaction mechanism as lithium ion batteries (LIBs), rich sodium resources, low cost, and environmental friendliness, have been regarded as suitable for grid-scale applications for secondary batteries. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref2 ref3" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref2 ref3" aria-label="reference 2 and 3">(2,3)</a> As the radius of Na<sup>+</sup> is larger than that of Li<sup>+</sup>, it makes the kinetics of Na<sup>+</sup> sluggish in the alloying/dealloying process, leading to poor rate capability and low power density, and prevents its commercial application. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref4 ref5" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref4 ref5" aria-label="reference 4 and 5">(4,5)</a> Therefore, it is most urgent to explore negative electrode materials with high energy density and rate capacity for SIBs.</div><div class="NLM_p">Sn-based anode materials have been considered as promising anode materials for SIBs because of their high theoretical capacity (∼847 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>), volumetric capacity (1210 Ah L<sup>–1</sup>) (based on the formation of Na<sub>15</sub>Sn<sub>4</sub>), low operation voltage (0.3–0.4 V), <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref5 ref6" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref5 ref6" aria-label="reference 5 and 6">(5,6)</a> high electronic conductivity, and good safety under ambient conditions. However, the main obstacle to the further development of Sn-based anode materials is the pulverization and agglomeration of electrode materials during sodiation/desodiation, which causes a serious volume change (410%) after full sodiation, leading to electrochemical inactivation for the active material and severe capacity attenuation upon cycling. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref7 ref8" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref7 ref8" aria-label="reference 7 and 8">(7,8)</a> To circumvent these problems, great efforts have been made to develop various Sn-based components and structures for SIBs. For example, our group synthesized uniform ultra-fine SbSn nanodots encapsulated in nitrogen-containing porous carbon nanofibers (SbSn@NCNFs) by electrospinning. When used as SIBs, SbSn@NCNFs could deliver a reversible capacity as high as 331 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> after 500 cycles at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref9" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref9" aria-label="reference 9">(9)</a> Chen and co-workers demonstrated that the heterostructure engineering of core–shelled Sb@Sb<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> encapsulated in three-dimensional (3D) N-doped carbon hollow spheres could retain a reversible capacity of 379 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> after 1000 cycles at 5 A g<sup>–1</sup>. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref10" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref10" aria-label="reference 10">(10)</a> Clearly, the most important feature of these materials is that a bimetallic alloy (SbSn) is selected to alleviate the internal stress generated and maintain the structural stability during the repeated Na-ion insertion/extraction processes. However, the huge volume change (Sn ↔ Na<sub>15</sub>Sn<sub>4</sub>: 520%, Sb ↔ Na<sub>3</sub>Sb: 390%) <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref11 ref12" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref11 ref12" aria-label="reference 11 and 12">(11,12)</a> during the charging/discharging process leads to intense pulverization, which reduces the contact between the electrolyte and the active substance and injures the cycle stability. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref13" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref13" aria-label="reference 13">(13)</a> Recently, a few reports have demonstrated that combining alloy Sn with other metals (Ni, Co, Cu) is a promising method to alleviate the volume expansion during the charging/discharging process. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref14 ref15 ref16" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref14 ref15 ref16" aria-label="reference 14 to 16">(14−16)</a> This is due to the Ni or the Co acting as an electrochemically inactive matrix not participating in the alloying reaction, which can not only buffer the volume variations but also inhibit aggregation and particle growth of the Sn phase during the electrochemical Na–Sn alloying process. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref14" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref14" aria-label="reference 14">(14)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">Another promising strategy toward obtaining a significant volume change is to prepare nanocomposite structures consisting of Sn nanoparticles and carbon: for example, carbon nanofibers or nanotubes, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref17 ref18" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref17 ref18" aria-label="reference 17 and 18">(17,18)</a> three-dimensional (3D) carbon matrixes, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref19" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref19" aria-label="reference 19">(19)</a> or graphene layers. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref20" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref20" aria-label="reference 20">(20)</a> Carbon nanofibers, specifically one-dimensional (1D) carbon nanofibers <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref21" aria-label="reference 21">(21)</a> with a hierarchical porous structure and flexible properties, have attracted much attention due to their excellent electron conduction channels, high specific surface area, and capability to alleviate volume change. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref22 ref23" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref22 ref23" aria-label="reference 22 and 23">(22,23)</a> In the construction of nanofiber structures, the electrospinning technology has attracted much attention due to its simple manufacturing process and low cost. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref24" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref24" aria-label="reference 24">(24)</a> Most importantly, the freestanding membrane obtained by electrospinning can be directly used as a negative electrode without adding the conductive agent and binder, which improves the energy density of the negative anode and avoids the failure and collapse of active materials during the charging and discharging process. Most importantly, the introduction of nitrogen by polyacrylonitrile (PAN) in the nanofiber can further enhance the electronic conductivity, due to which many carbon defects are introduced. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref25" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref25" aria-label="reference 25">(25)</a> On the other hand, the introduction of hollow carbon spheres (HCSs) can provide more buffer space during the alloying/dealloying process. Meanwhile, the HCSs with a mesoporous structure and larger specific surface area can enhance the interface contact with the electrolyte to accelerate the diffusion transfer of electrons and ions.</div><div class="NLM_p last">In this context, we reported the synthesis of SnCo particles encapsulated in integrated carbon matrix-synergized N-doped carbon fibers with hollow carbon spheres (B-SnCo/NCFs) as anodes for SIBs, by means of electrospinning followed by carbonization treatment. The HCSs serve as nanoreactors and can control the confined growth of SnCo nanoparticles and prevent SnCo from agglomeration during the formation process to improve the cycle stability of the battery. The ultrasmall Sn nanocrystals and HCSs enable fast Na<sup>+</sup> transportation and easy strain relaxation. The B-SnCo/NCF CNF-based SIBs manifest a set of noteworthy electrochemical properties, including a large specific capacity, excellent cycling stability, and outstanding rate performance, and, notably, the reversible capacity of 351 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup> after 300 cycles.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i3">2.  Experimental Section</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec2_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i4" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i4">2.1.  Materials Synthesis</h3><div class="NLM_p">Precursor SiO<sub>2</sub>@SiO<sub>2</sub>/RF nanospheres were synthesized by co-condensation of tetraethyl orthosilicate (TEOS) and resorcinol formaldehyde oligomer on SiO<sub>2</sub> surface. Firstly, 3.5 mL of TEOS was added into a mixed solution containing deionized water (10 mL), ethanol (70 mL), and ammonia solution (3.5 mL, 25 wt %) under stirring vigorously at room temperature. After stirring for 15 min, formaldehyde (0.56 mL) and resorcinol (0.4 g) were added into the above solution and stirred for 24 h at room temperature. The SiO<sub>2</sub>@SiO<sub>2</sub>/RF nanospheres were obtained by centrifugation, washed with deionized water and ethanol several times, and dried in a vacuum oven at 80 °C for 12 h. Second, the precursor of SiO<sub>2</sub>@SiO<sub>2</sub>/RF nanospheres was calcinated under Ar atmosphere to 650 °C for 5 h to obtain the SiO<sub>2</sub>@SiO<sub>2</sub>/C nanospheres. Finally, the HCSs were obtained through sodium hydroxide (NaOH) etching.</div><div class="NLM_p">First, 0.5 g of polyacrylonitrile (PAN, <i>M</i><sub>w</sub> = 150,000, Aldrich), 0.1 g of HCSs, 0.238 g of cobalt dichloride hexahydrate (CoCl<sub>2</sub>·6H<sub>2</sub>O), and 0.226 g of Tin(II) chloride dihydrate (SnCl<sub>2</sub>·2H<sub>2</sub>O) were dissolved in dimethylformamide (DMF) (99.8%) under vigorous stirring at 60 °C for 3 h. Then, the solution was transferred to a 5 mL plastic syringe equipped with a 20-gauge stainless-steel needle for electrospinning at a feed speed of 0.6 mL h<sup>–1</sup> and applied voltage of 15 kV, and the distance between the needle and the collector was maintained at 18 cm. The obtained as-spun fibers were dried at 60 °C overnight in a vacuum oven. Subsequently, the obtained nanofiber membrane was stabilized in air at 250 °C for 2 h, and then carbonized at 600 °C for 2 h with 2 °C min<sup>–1</sup> in the gas flow of Ar/H<sub>2</sub> (95 vs 5 vol %). Finally, the B-SnCo/NCFs were obtained. For the sake of contrast, the control samples, the B-Sn/NCFs, Sn/NCFs, and CoSn/NCFs were obtained.</div><div class="NLM_p last">The procedure for synthesizing CoSn/NCFs was similar to the B-SnCo/NCFs method except for the removal of HCSs. First, 0.5 g of polyacrylonitrile (PAN, <i>M</i><sub>w</sub> = 150,000, Aldrich), cobalt dichloride hexahydrate (CoCl<sub>2</sub>·6H<sub>2</sub>O), and 0.226 g of Tin(II) chloride dihydrate (SnCl<sub>2</sub>·2H<sub>2</sub>O) were dissolved in DMF (99.8%) under vigorous stirring at 60 °C for 3 h. Then, the solution was transferred to the 5 mL plastic syringe equipped with a 20-gauge stainless-steel needle for electrospinning at a feed speed of 0.6 mL h<sup>–1</sup> and an applied voltage of 15 kV, and the distance between the needle and the collector was maintained at 18 cm. The obtained as-spun fibers were dried at 60 °C overnight in a vacuum oven. Subsequently, the obtained nanofiber membrane was stabilized in air at 250 °C for 2 h, and then carbonized at 600 °C for 2 h with 2 °C min<sup>–1</sup> in the gas flow of Ar/H<sub>2</sub> (95 vs 5 vol %). Finally, the SnCo/NCFs were obtained.</div></div><div id="sec2_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i5" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i5">2.2.  Material Characterization</h3><div class="NLM_p last">Phase structure was obtained using a Bruker D8 ADVANCE X-ray powder diffractometer in the 2θ range from 10 to 80 under Cu Kα radiation (λ = 0.15418 nm). The morphologies and structures of the products were investigated by scanning electron microscopy (SEM, HITACHI SU8010) and transmission electron microscopy (TEM, FEI Talos F200X) at an accelerating voltage of 200 kV. The elemental composition and chemical state of the samples were detected by X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) analysis using a PHI5000 Versa Probe III XPS with an Al Kα excitation source. N<sub>2</sub> adsorption–desorption isotherms were obtained by using Brunauer–Emmett–Teller (BET, ASAP 2020 PLUS HD88). Thermogravimetric analysis (TGA) was carried out to calculate the carbon contents of the products using 600 SDT under room temperature to 900 °C temperature range in air. Raman spectra were studied using a dispersive Raman microscope (XPLORA PLUS) with a wavelength of 532 nm.</div></div><div id="sec2_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i6" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i6">2.3.  Electrochemical Measurements</h3><div class="NLM_p last">Electrochemical measurements of the products were conducted using CR2025 coin-type cells assembled in an Ar-filled glovebox. The working electrodes were prepared by mixing the active materials (80 wt %), acetylene black (10 wt %), and poly(vinylidene fluoride) (PVDF, 10 wt %) in <i>N</i>-methyl-2-pyrrolidinone (NMP) to form a slurry. The slurry was coated onto Ni foam, which was pressed at 20 MPa to result in good contact between them, and then dried at 80 °C in a vacuum overnight. The mass loading of the active material was 1.2 mg cm<sup>–2</sup>. The SIB electrolyte solution was 1 M NaClO<sub>4</sub> dissolved in a mixed solution of propylene carbonate (PC)/ethylene carbonate (EC) (PC/EC = 1:1) with 5 wt % fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC) as the additive. Cyclic voltammetry (CV) measurements were performed between 0.005 and 3.0 V at a scan rate from 0.1 to 2.0 mV s<sup>–1</sup> and the electrochemical impedance spectrum (EIS) measurements were carried out at room temperature within the frequency range from 0.01 to 100 kHz using a CHI 660D electrochemical workstation. The charge–discharge tests were performed in a cutoff potential window of 0.005–3.0 V using a LAND battery program-control test system after aging for more than 10 h.</div></div></div><div id="sec3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i7">3.  Results and Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">The synthesis route of bean pod-like B-SnCo/NCFs is illustrated in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>. First, the hollow carbon spheres (HCSs) were obtained according to previous literature. Briefly, tetraethylorthosilicate (TEOS) and resorcinol formaldehyde (RF) oligomers were co-condensed on the SiO<sub>2</sub> surface to form SiO<sub>2</sub>@SiO<sub>2</sub>/RF nanospheres. As-prepared SiO<sub>2</sub>@SiO<sub>2</sub>/RF nanospheres were annealed at 650 °C under Ar to obtain SiO<sub>2</sub>@SiO<sub>2</sub>/C nanospheres. The hollow carbon spheres (HCSs) were obtained by etching SiO<sub>2</sub> using NaOH. <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646/suppl_file/ic3c00646_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S1a,b</a> shows the scanning electron microscope (SEM) and transmission electron microscope (TEM) images of HCSs, respectively. Then, the precursor solution of HCSs, polyacrylonitrile (PAN), and metal chlorides in DMF (<i>N</i>,<i>N</i>-dimethylformamide) was embedded into as-spun PAN/HCSs/SnCl<sub>2</sub>·2H<sub>2</sub>O/CoCl<sub>2</sub>·6H<sub>2</sub>O fibers by electrospinning. Subsequently, the collected nanofiber membranes were carbonized in air atmosphere at 250 °C and further reduced at 600 °C under the atmosphere of Ar/H<sub>2</sub>, yielding the B-SnCo/NCFs membrane. During carbonization, the SnCl<sub>2</sub>·2H<sub>2</sub>O and CoCl<sub>2</sub>·6H<sub>2</sub>O were reduced to SnCo nanoparticles, and polyacrylonitrile (PAN) was converted to N-doped multichannel carbon nanofibers. It is worth mentioning that HCSs can not only improve the conductivity but also prevent SnCo agglomeration during the formation process.</div><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646/asset/images/medium/ic3c00646_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646/asset/images/large/ic3c00646_0002.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. Schematic illustration for the synthesis process of the B-SnCo/NCFs.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646/asset/images/large/ic3c00646_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">The morphology, structure, and chemical composition of the B-SnCo/NCF membrane was characterized by SEM, TEM, and X-ray diffraction (XRD). <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>a shows the images of the precursor nanofiber membrane of PAN/HCSs/SnCl<sub>2</sub>·2H<sub>2</sub>O/CoCl<sub>2</sub>·6H<sub>2</sub>O. The diameter of the nanofiber precursor is about 500 nm and HCSs are evenly embedded in the nanofiber. The surface light of the nanofiber can be clearly seen because SnCo nanoparticles are not reduced. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>b,c shows the SEM images of B-SnCo/NCFs. After carbonization, the SnCo nanoparticles were encapsulated in the HCSs and the diameter of the nanofiber was decreased by around 450 nm compared with the precursor nanofiber. This is because the polymers and reduced ionic salts were decomposed during the high-temperature calcination process. X-ray diffraction characterization was used to examine the crystal characteristics and phase information of B-SnCo/NCFs, SnCo/NCFs, B-Sn/NCFs, and Sn/NCFs. The XRD pattern of B-SnCo/NCFs (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>d) indicates that the diffraction peaks located at 28.5, 33.9, and 45.1° could be well ascribed to the (101), (110), and (201) planes of SnCo alloy (JCPDS No.02-0559); <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref26" aria-label="reference 26">(26)</a> no other phases were found in the XRD spectra of B-SnCo/NCF and SnCo/NCF (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646/suppl_file/ic3c00646_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2</a>) samples. Meanwhile, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646/suppl_file/ic3c00646_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S3</a> presents the XRD pattern of Sn/NCFs, in which all peaks are assigned as the Sn phase (JCPDS. No 04-0673). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref27" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref27" aria-label="reference 27">(27)</a> <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>e shows the low-magnification TEM image of B-SnCo/NCFs, which indicates that HCSs are well distributed inside the nitrogen-doped carbon nanofibers, and SnCo nanoparticles are grown uniformly on the HCSs inside instead of agglomerating, with a diameter of 100 nm, to form a bean pod-like structure of SnCo/N-doped carbon nanofibers. The high-resolution TEM (HRTEM) image of B-SnCo/NCFs (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>f) clearly reveals that the lattice spacing of 0.31 nm is consistent with the (101) lattice facets of SnCo. Additionally, the corresponding selected area electron diffraction (SAED) is shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>g. The concentric diffraction ring agrees with the phases of SnCo. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>h–l shows the energy-dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDX) mapping test of B-SnCo/NCFs. It is observed that the elements of C, N and Sn, Co are homogeneously distributed throughout the carbon nanofibers and HCS, respectively, which further proves the uniform growth of SnCo nanoparticles inside the HCS and the uniform distribution of N-doped carbon nanofibers in the HCS to improve the conductivity of the anodes.</div><figure id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646/asset/images/medium/ic3c00646_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646/asset/images/large/ic3c00646_0003.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. (a) SEM image of as-spun PAN/HCSs/SnCl<sub>2</sub>·2H<sub>2</sub>O/CoCl<sub>2</sub>·6H<sub>2</sub>O, (b, c) SEM images of B-SnCo/NCFs, (d) XRD pattern of B-SnCo/NCFs, (e) TEM image, (f) HRTEM image, (g) SAED image, and (h–l) TEM-EDS images of B-SnCo/NCFs.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646/asset/images/large/ic3c00646_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">By slightly modifying the synthesis conditions, the three samples SnCo/NCFs, B-Sn/NCFs, and Sn/NCFs can also be synthesized (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>). <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>a,b shows the SEM and TEM images of the morphology of SnCo/NCFs, respectively, where SnCo nanoparticles with an average diameter of 20 nm are uniformly embedded into N-doped carbon nanofibers, and no apparent SnCo nanoparticles are aggregated on the carbon nanofibers. The TEM-EDX elemental-mapping images, shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>c, reveal the homogeneous distribution of C, N, Sn, and Co elements in SnCo/NCFs. Meanwhile, <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>f–i reveals the TEM-EDX elemental-mapping images of B-Sn/NCFs and Sn/NCFs, respectively. Moreover, <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>d–e,<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>g–h reveals the SEM and TEM images of the morphology of B-Sn/NCFs and Sn/NCFs, respectively. Most importantly, this unique synthesis strategy can provide a reference for synthesizing other pod-like beans of Sn-based anode materials. The HRTEM shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646/suppl_file/ic3c00646_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S4a,b</a> displays the lattice fringes with a d-spacing of around 0.31 nm, which can be assigned to the (101) planes of hexagonal SnCo (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646/suppl_file/ic3c00646_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S4c</a>). <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646/suppl_file/ic3c00646_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S5a,b</a> presents the HRTEM image of the synthesized Sn/NCFs. The interplanar distance is 0.29 nm, which is consistent with the (200) plane of Sn, and the concentric diffraction ring agrees with the multiphases of Sn, being consistent with the XRD results, as shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646/suppl_file/ic3c00646_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S5c</a>.</div><figure id="fig3" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646/asset/images/medium/ic3c00646_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646/asset/images/large/ic3c00646_0004.jpeg" id="gr3" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. (a) SEM image and (b) TEM image, (c) TEM-EDS images of SnCo/NCFs, (d) SEM image and (e) TEM image, (f) TEM-EDS images of B-Sn/NCFs, (g) SEM image and (h) TEM image, and (i) EM-EDS images of Sn/NCFs.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646/asset/images/large/ic3c00646_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.inorgchem.3c00646&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">In order to confirm the carbon content in B-SnCo/NCFs, thermogravimetric analysis (TGA) was carried out. As shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>a, the slight weight decreases before 200 °C can be attributed to the evaporation of the water in B-SnCo/NCFs. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref28" aria-label="reference 28">(28)</a> Then, the main loss between 300 and 600 °C can be attributed to the combustion of carbon material and the oxidation of SnCo to form SnO<sub>2</sub> and Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub>. The content of SnCo in B-SnCo/NCFs is calculated as 34.8% by the following equation <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref29" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref29" aria-label="reference 29">(29)</a><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq1"><div class="equation"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"></span><div class="MathJax_Display" style="text-align: left;"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0" data-mathml="<math xmlns=&quot;http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML&quot; width: 0px; height: 2.219em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.247em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.066em;"></span></span></nobr><span class="MJX_Assistive_MathML MJX_Assistive_MathML_Block" role="presentation"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi><mo>+</mo><msub><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">O</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msub></mstyle></mrow></mrow><mrow><mo linebreak="nobreak">→</mo><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><msub><mrow><mi>CO</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msub></mstyle></mrow></math></span></span></div><script type="math/mml" id="MathJax-Element-1"><math display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi><mo>+</mo><msub><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">O</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msub></mstyle></mrow></mrow><mrow><mo linebreak="nobreak">→</mo><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><msub><mrow><mi>CO</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msub></mstyle></mrow></math></script></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(1)</span></div></div><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq2"><div class="equation"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"></span><div class="MathJax_Display" style="text-align: left;"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0" data-mathml="<math xmlns=&quot;http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML&quot;
